</style><script type="application/ld+json" data-next-head="">{"@context":"https://schema.org","@type":"BlogPosting","datePublished":"3/25/2021, 7:00:35 PM","description":"In&amp;nbsp;this&amp;nbsp;blog post we will&amp;nbsp;provide&amp;nbsp;Microsoft&amp;nbsp;Azure Sentinel&amp;nbsp;customers with&amp;nbsp;hunting queries to&amp;nbsp;investigate&amp;nbsp;possible&amp;nbsp;on-premises&amp;nbsp;Exchange&amp;nbsp;Server&amp;nbsp;exploitation and identify&amp;nbsp;additional&amp;nbsp;attacker&amp;nbsp;IOCs (Indicators of compromise)&amp;nbsp;such as IP address and User Agent.&amp;nbsp;These hunting techniques can also be applied to web shell&amp;nbsp;techniques targeting other web applications.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe&amp;nbsp;techniques&amp;nbsp;we discuss below&amp;nbsp;have been&amp;nbsp;adapted from the&amp;nbsp;June 2020 blog post:&amp;nbsp;Web shell threat hunting with Azure Sentinel and Microsoft Threat Protection. The previous blog post analysed an&amp;nbsp;attack&amp;nbsp;against&amp;nbsp;a SharePoint&amp;nbsp;server,&amp;nbsp;however,&amp;nbsp;many of the techniques&amp;nbsp;can also be applied&amp;nbsp;to Exchange&amp;nbsp;servers&amp;nbsp;since it also uses IIS to host its web interfaces.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nRecent vulnerabilities in&amp;nbsp;on-premises&amp;nbsp;Microsoft Exchange&amp;nbsp;servers&amp;nbsp;have led to deployment of web shells by threat actors.&amp;nbsp;More information on these vulnerabilities&amp;nbsp;can be found&amp;nbsp;in this&amp;nbsp;MSRC&amp;nbsp;blog,&amp;nbsp;details on&amp;nbsp;threat actor&amp;nbsp;HAFNIUM using these vulnerabilities can be found in this&amp;nbsp;MSTIC&amp;nbsp;blog.&amp;nbsp;MSRC has also provided&amp;nbsp;guidance for responders, a&amp;nbsp;one-click&amp;nbsp;tool for remediation and automatic remediation is delivered through Microsoft Defender for Endpoint.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nOur colleagues in Microsoft Defender Threat Intelligence have authored another blog that&amp;nbsp;provides additional details on&amp;nbsp;use of web shells&amp;nbsp;in attacks taking advantage of the Exchange Server.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe below diagram provides a high-level overview of&amp;nbsp;an&amp;nbsp;attacker&amp;nbsp;leveraging these vulnerabilities to&amp;nbsp;install&amp;nbsp;a&amp;nbsp;web shell on an Exchange server.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\n\n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nInvestigating web shell alerts&amp;nbsp;\nMicrosoft 365 Defender (M365D)&amp;nbsp;detects&amp;nbsp;web shell installation&amp;nbsp;and execution&amp;nbsp;activity. Security alerts&amp;nbsp;and incidents&amp;nbsp;generated by M365D&amp;nbsp;can be&amp;nbsp;written to the SecurityAlert table in Azure Sentinel&amp;nbsp;by enabling the&amp;nbsp;appropriate connector. An example of a web shell installation alert in the Azure Sentinel SecurityAlert table can be seen below.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\n\n&amp;nbsp;\nThese alerts can be&amp;nbsp;enriched&amp;nbsp;in Azure Sentinel&amp;nbsp;with&amp;nbsp;new&amp;nbsp;information&amp;nbsp;from other log sources.&amp;nbsp;When dealing with&amp;nbsp;remote&amp;nbsp;attacks on web application servers,&amp;nbsp;one of the best&amp;nbsp;enrichment sources available are&amp;nbsp;the&amp;nbsp;web logs that have been generated. In the case that the application server is Microsoft Exchange the W3CIISLog can be used to enrich M365D alerts with potential attacker information.&amp;nbsp;Information on collecting IIS logs using the Log Analytics agent can be found&amp;nbsp;here.\n&amp;nbsp;\nIdentifying the Attacker IP address&amp;nbsp;from&amp;nbsp;Microsoft&amp;nbsp;365&amp;nbsp;Defender&amp;nbsp;alerts&amp;nbsp;\nThe query below extracts&amp;nbsp;alerts from M365D&amp;nbsp;where a web&amp;nbsp;script&amp;nbsp;file has been observed as part of the alert. In the below example,&amp;nbsp;alerts containing&amp;nbsp;ASP,&amp;nbsp;ASPX, ASMX and ASAX files will be extracted;&amp;nbsp;these are web script files&amp;nbsp;commonly used&amp;nbsp;by&amp;nbsp;Exchange servers.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nAfter extracting relevant web shell alerts the query will join the alert information with the W3CIIS log, this allows the query to identify any clients that have accessed the potential shell file, allowing&amp;nbsp;the potential&amp;nbsp;attacker to be identified.&amp;nbsp;A version of the query below is already available as an Azure Sentinel detection and can be&amp;nbsp;found here.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nlet timeWindow = 3d; \n//Script file extensions to match on, can be expanded for your environment \nlet scriptExtensions = dynamic([&quot;.asp&quot;, &quot;.aspx&quot;, &quot;.asmx&quot;, &quot;.asax&quot;]); \nSecurityAlert \n| where TimeGenerated &amp;gt; ago(timeWindow) \n| where ProviderName == &quot;MDATP&quot; \n//Parse and expand the alert JSON \n| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) \n| mvexpand alertData \n| where alertData.Type == &quot;file&quot; \n//This can be expanded to include more file types \n| where alertData.Name has_any(scriptExtensions) \n| extend FileName = tostring(alertData.Name), Directory = tostring(alertData.Directory) \n| project TimeGenerated, FileName, Directory \n| join (  \nW3CIISLog  \n| where TimeGenerated &amp;gt; ago(timeWindow)  \n| where csUriStem has_any(scriptExtensions)  \n| extend splitUriStem = split(csUriStem, &quot;/&quot;)  \n| extend FileName = splitUriStem[-1] \n| summarize StartTime=min(TimeGenerated), EndTime=max(TimeGenerated) by AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUserAgent=csUserAgent, SiteName=sSiteName, ShellLocation=csUriStem, tostring(FileName)  \n) on FileName \n| project StartTime, EndTime, AttackerIP, AttackerUserAgent, SiteName, ShellLocation \n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nIdentifying Exchange&amp;nbsp;Servers &amp;amp; Associated&amp;nbsp;Security Alerts&amp;nbsp;\nExchange servers can&amp;nbsp;be challenging to identify in&amp;nbsp;default log data;&amp;nbsp;however&amp;nbsp;using data available in W3CIISLog,&amp;nbsp;Exchange servers can be identified using predictable URI strings without relying&amp;nbsp;on the&amp;nbsp;hostname or site name.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe query below&amp;nbsp;extracts&amp;nbsp;the host name from W3CIISLog where a known&amp;nbsp;Exchange URI path is observed, this provides a list of hostnames that are running Exchange. This list of host names can then be used to&amp;nbsp;aggregate information from the&amp;nbsp;alerts in the&amp;nbsp;SecurityAlert&amp;nbsp;table.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nW3CIISLog \n| where csUriStem has_any(&quot;/owa/auth/&quot;, &quot;/ecp/healthcheck.htm&quot;, &quot;/ews/exchange.asmx&quot;) \n| summarize by computer=tolower(Computer) \n| join kind=leftouter ( \nSecurityAlert \n| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) \n| mvexpand alertData \n| where alertData.Type == &quot;host&quot; \n| extend computer = iff(isnotempty(alertData.DnsDomain), tolower(strcat(tostring(alertData.HostName), &quot;.&quot; , tostring(alertData.DnsDomain))),tolower(tostring(alertData.HostName))) \n| summarize Alerts=dcount(SystemAlertId), AlertTimes=make_list(TimeGenerated), AlertNames=make_list(AlertName) by computer \n) on computer \n| project ExchangeServer=computer, Alerts, AlertTimes, AlertNames \n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\n\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe results of the query provide insights into&amp;nbsp;whether&amp;nbsp;additional security alerts beyond web shell alerts have been observed on the host.&amp;nbsp;Following deployment of a web shell it’s highly likely the threat actor will begin to execute further commands on the server, triggering additional alerts.&amp;nbsp;In the above example three Exchange servers were observed with security alerts.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThis same technique can be used to locate other web applications&amp;nbsp;within the network that use common or predictable web paths.\n&amp;nbsp;\nW3CIISLog Analysis&amp;nbsp;\nW3CIISLog&amp;nbsp;provides detailed logging on actions performed on Microsoft&amp;nbsp;Internet Information Servers (IIS).&amp;nbsp;Even when an&amp;nbsp;Endpoint detection&amp;nbsp;alert is not&amp;nbsp;available,&amp;nbsp;it is possible to explore W3CIISLogs for indicators of compromise.&amp;nbsp;W3CIISLog can also provide additional insights into which hosts&amp;nbsp;in the network&amp;nbsp;are web application servers.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nNote:&amp;nbsp;As part of the original Microsoft&amp;nbsp;HAFNIUM blog post, several hunting and detection queries were created to search for&amp;nbsp;artefacts specific to the use of recent vulnerabilities.\n&amp;nbsp;\nIdentifying&amp;nbsp;generic exploitation activity&amp;nbsp;\nIf the URI associated with the vulnerable file on the server is known,&amp;nbsp;a query can be constructed to&amp;nbsp;identify log entries that match the URI pattern.&amp;nbsp;W3CIIS&amp;nbsp;logging&amp;nbsp;stores the URI in the column&amp;nbsp;named&amp;nbsp;“csUriStem”, the below query can be used to search for a specific URI&amp;nbsp;in&amp;nbsp;logs and provide information on which clients have accessed them.&amp;nbsp;Local IP addresses have been removed.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nW3CIISLog \n| where TimeGenerated &amp;gt; ago(3d) \n| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) \n//Insert potentially exploited URI here \n| where csUriStem =~ &quot;/owa/auth/x.js&quot; \n| project TimeGenerated, sSiteName, csMethod, csUriStem, sPort, cIP, csUserAgent \n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\n\n&amp;nbsp;\nFor HAFNIUM attacks observed by MSTIC an indicator feed has been&amp;nbsp;made available&amp;nbsp;(CSV,&amp;nbsp;JSON). A&amp;nbsp;detection query,&amp;nbsp;that&amp;nbsp;will check for the presence of indicators in multiple data sources, has also been made available by the Azure Sentinel team. The&amp;nbsp;detection&amp;nbsp;can be found&amp;nbsp;here, and IOC’s&amp;nbsp;released as feeds by MSTIC&amp;nbsp;can be found in this&amp;nbsp;directory.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe recent&amp;nbsp;Exchange vulnerabilities&amp;nbsp;do not need to be targeted at a specific file.&amp;nbsp;Analysis of automated exploitation tools online shows that many randomise the filenames used;&amp;nbsp;this means that no legitimate user will visit these files as they do not exist on the server. As these filenames are randomly generated, static string matching cannot be used.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe Kusto “matches_regex” function can be used to perform regular expression matching on URI’s. The below example extracts events&amp;nbsp;where the URI matches&amp;nbsp;files associated with the exploitation of&amp;nbsp;CVE-2021-27065&amp;nbsp;from W3CIISLog.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nW3CIISLog \n| where TimeGenerated &amp;gt; ago(3d) \n| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) \n| where (csUriStem matches regex @&quot;\\/owa\\/auth\\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\\.js&quot;) or (csUriStem matches regex @&quot;\\/ecp\\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\\.(js|flt|css)&quot;) \n| project TimeGenerated, sSiteName, csMethod, csUriStem, sPort, cIP, csUserAgent\n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\n\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe previous queries can be limited when the files being exploited are&amp;nbsp;commonly accessed. They would produce many candidate attacker IP addresses, making analysis&amp;nbsp;challenging.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nUsing the recent Exchange vulnerabilities as an example,&amp;nbsp;Microsoft has&amp;nbsp;seen&amp;nbsp;malicious&amp;nbsp;automated&amp;nbsp;tools&amp;nbsp;released publicly that are being&amp;nbsp;used&amp;nbsp;to&amp;nbsp;exploit&amp;nbsp;the Exchange&amp;nbsp;vulnerabilities. These tools are designed to&amp;nbsp;only visit&amp;nbsp;specific&amp;nbsp;URIs on the server that are required to perform the exploit. This activity differs from&amp;nbsp;normal and&amp;nbsp;legitimate Administrator or User&amp;nbsp;application&amp;nbsp;browsing&amp;nbsp;activity&amp;nbsp;and if observed should be investigated.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nIt is possible to craft a query that uses basic statistical analysis to identify instances where a client has visited a disproportionately high number of exploit-related URI’s when compared to other URIs on the site.,&amp;nbsp;The query below calculates the&amp;nbsp;total number of suspicious URIs&amp;nbsp;that&amp;nbsp;have been visited by each user, it then calculates the total number of URIs visited by the user. Where the number of exploit&amp;nbsp;related&amp;nbsp;URIs is&amp;nbsp;a significant proportion of URIs visited, a result is returned.&amp;nbsp;By&amp;nbsp;default,&amp;nbsp;the query requires over 90% of the URIs visited by the user to be suspicious.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nlet timeRange = 7d;\n//Calculate number of suspicious URI stems visited by user \nW3CIISLog\n| where TimeGenerated &amp;gt; ago(timeRange)\n| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) \n| where (csUriStem matches regex @&quot;\\/owa\\/auth\\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\\.js&quot;) or (csUriStem matches regex @&quot;\\/ecp\\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\\.(js|flt|css)&quot;) or (csUriStem =~ &quot;/ews/exchange.asmx&quot;) \n| extend userHash = hash_md5(strcat(cIP, csUserAgent)) \n| summarize susCount=dcount(csUriStem), make_list(csUriStem), min(TimeGenerated), max(TimeGenerated) by userHash, cIP, csUserAgent \n| join kind=leftouter  ( \n//Calculate unique URI stems visited by each user \nW3CIISLog \n| where TimeGenerated &amp;gt; ago(timeRange) \n| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP))\n| extend userHash = hash_md5(strcat(cIP, csUserAgent)) \n| summarize allCount=dcount(csUriStem) by userHash \n) on userHash \n//Find instances where only a common endpoint was seen \n| extend containsDefault = iff(list_csUriStem contains &quot;/ews/exchange.asmx&quot;, 1, 0) \n//If we only see the common endpoint and nothing else dump it \n| extend result = iff(containsDefault == 1, containsDefault+susCount, 0) \n| where result != 2 \n| extend susPercentage = susCount / allCount * 100 \n| where susPercentage &amp;gt; 90 \n| project StartTime=min_TimeGenerated, EndTime=max_TimeGenerated, AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUA=csUserAgent, URIsVisited=list_csUriStem, suspiciousPercentage=susPercentage, allUriCount=allCount, suspiciousUriCount=susCount\n&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nWhile this query is designed to detect recent Exchange exploit activity, it can be easily adapted to&amp;nbsp;other exploit chains if the pages or URIs used are known.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nRare Client File Access&amp;nbsp;\nA previously published&amp;nbsp;hunting query&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;can be used to detect instances where resources on a server are requested by a single client&amp;nbsp;– a&amp;nbsp;behaviour&amp;nbsp;that should be investigated in the context of web shell&amp;nbsp;exploits.&amp;nbsp;After&amp;nbsp;the actor&amp;nbsp;creates&amp;nbsp;web&amp;nbsp;shell&amp;nbsp;on&amp;nbsp;the&amp;nbsp;server, it’s likely that they will be the only user to access the file&amp;nbsp;to complete their intended objective.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nInvestigating the Attacker&amp;nbsp;\nIn the&amp;nbsp;previous&amp;nbsp;blog post&amp;nbsp;covering SharePoint&amp;nbsp;exploitation,&amp;nbsp;a Jupyter&amp;nbsp;Notebook&amp;nbsp;Guided Investigation is provided. This notebook can also be used to investigate&amp;nbsp;on-prem&amp;nbsp;Exchange compromises&amp;nbsp;within your environment.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nThe notebook extracts&amp;nbsp;alerts from Microsoft 365 Defender related to web shell activity,&amp;nbsp;these can then be enriched with information from W3CIIS to identify the attacker IP and User Agent.&amp;nbsp;The attackers IP and User Agent can be used to hunt through multiple log sources for potential post-compromise activity.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nAfter the attacker details have been identified,&amp;nbsp;the notebook can be used to&amp;nbsp;locate&amp;nbsp;files that were accessed by the attacker prior to the web shell being installed. The notebook will also&amp;nbsp;locate the first instance that the attacker visited the server.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nAzure-Sentinel-Notebooks/Guided Investigation - MDE Webshell Alerts.ipynb at master · Azure/Azure-Sentinel-Notebooks (github.com)&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nInstructions for getting the notebook up and&amp;nbsp;running can be&amp;nbsp;found in the&amp;nbsp;original blog post, under the title “Building out the Investigation using Jupyter Notebooks”.&amp;nbsp;\n&amp;nbsp;\nYou can stay up to date&amp;nbsp;with the latest information at&amp;nbsp;https://aka.ms/exchangevulns.&amp;nbsp;","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/microsoftsentinelblog/web-shell-threat-hunting-with-azure-sentinel/2234968"},"headline":"Web Shell Threat Hunting with Azure Sentinel","image":["https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yMjM0OTY4LTI2NzAwNmlFNkRFNUU1MTY2NzBDRDM1?revision=6"],"dateModified":"3/25/2021, <P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">T</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">he</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>techniques<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">we discuss below<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">have been<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">adapted from the</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>June 2020 blog post</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">:</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW114348115 BCX8" href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/azure-sentinel/web-shell-threat-hunting-with-azure-sentinel-and-microsoft/ba-p/1448065" target="_blank"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114348115 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">Web shell threat hunting with Azure Sentinel and Microsoft Threat Protection</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">. The previous blog post analysed an</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">attack<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">against<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">a SharePoint<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">server,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">however,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>many of the techniques<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">can also be applied</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>to Exchange</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">servers</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">since it also uses IIS to host its web interfaces</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114348115 BCX8">.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW114348115 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Recent vulnerabilities in&nbsp;on-premises&nbsp;Microsoft Exchange&nbsp;servers&nbsp;have led to deployment of web shells by threat actors.&nbsp;More information on these vulnerabilities&nbsp;can be found&nbsp;in this&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2021/03/05/microsoft-exchange-server-vulnerabilities-mitigations-march-2021/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">MSRC&nbsp;blog</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">,&nbsp;details on&nbsp;threat actor&nbsp;HAFNIUM using these vulnerabilities can be found in this&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/03/02/hafnium-targeting-exchange-servers/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">MSTIC&nbsp;blog</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">.&nbsp;MSRC has also provided&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2021/03/16/guidance-for-responders-investigating-and-remediating-on-premises-exchange-server-vulnerabilities/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">guidance for responders</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="none">, a&nbsp;one-click&nbsp;tool for remediation and automatic remediation is delivered through Microsoft Defender for Endpoint</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast="auto">.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Our colleagues in Microsoft Defender Threat Intelligence have authored another blog that&nbsp;provides additional details on&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://aka.ms/exchange-threat-intelligence" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">use of web shells&nbsp;in attacks taking advantage of the Exchange Server</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The below diagram provides a high-level overview of&nbsp;an&nbsp;attacker&nbsp;leveraging these vulnerabilities to&nbsp;install&nbsp;a&nbsp;web shell on an Exchange server.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="diagram_2.PNG"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image diagram_2.PNG"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yMjM0OTY4LTI2Njk2OGk4QTlCNTM2RUJGRjEwREEw?image-dimensions=999x506&amp;revision=6" width="999" height="506" alt="diagram_2.PNG" /></button></span></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="1" id="community-2234968-toc-hId--497434982"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Investigating web shell alerts</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:240,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Microsoft 365 Defender (M365D)&nbsp;detects&nbsp;web shell installation&nbsp;and execution&nbsp;activity. Security alerts&nbsp;and incidents&nbsp;generated by M365D&nbsp;can be&nbsp;written to the SecurityAlert table in Azure Sentinel&nbsp;by enabling the&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/sentinel/connect-microsoft-365-defender" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">appropriate connector</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">. An example of a web shell installation alert in the Azure Sentinel SecurityAlert table can be seen below.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="Capture3.PNG"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image Capture3.PNG"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yMjM0OTY4LTI2Njk4OWk2QUYxMzA3QUM3RTIwOEU0?image-dimensions=647x359&amp;revision=6" width="647" height="359" alt="Capture3.PNG" /></button></span></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">These alerts can be</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>enriched<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">in Azure Sentinel<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">with<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">new<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">information</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>from other log sources</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">When dealing with</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>remote</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>attacks on web application servers</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">one of the best</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">enrichment sources available are</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">web logs that have been generated. In the case that the application server is Microsoft Exchange the W3CIISLog can be used to enrich M365D alerts with potential attacker information.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">Information on collecting IIS logs using the Log Analytics agent can be found<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink  BCX8 SCXW96846102" href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/azure-monitor/agents/data-sources-iis-logs" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined  BCX8 SCXW96846102" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">here</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW96846102">.</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2234968-toc-hId-1990077851"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Identifying the Attacker IP address&nbsp;from&nbsp;Microsoft&nbsp;365&nbsp;Defender&nbsp;alerts</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The query below extracts&nbsp;alerts from M365D&nbsp;where a web&nbsp;script&nbsp;file has been observed as part of the alert. In the below example,&nbsp;alerts containing&nbsp;ASP,&nbsp;ASPX, ASMX and ASAX files will be extracted;&nbsp;these are web script files&nbsp;commonly used&nbsp;by&nbsp;Exchange servers.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">After extracting relevant web shell alerts the query will join the alert information with the W3CIIS log, this allows the query to identify any clients that have accessed the potential shell file, allowing&nbsp;the potential&nbsp;attacker to be identified.&nbsp;A version of the query below is already available as an Azure Sentinel detection and can be&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/blob/master/Detections/W3CIISLog/MaliciousAlertLinkedWebRequests.yaml" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">found here</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-csharp"><code>let timeWindow = 3d; 
//Script file extensions to match on, can be expanded for your environment 
let scriptExtensions = dynamic([".asp", ".aspx", ".asmx", ".asax"]); 
SecurityAlert 
| where TimeGenerated &gt; ago(timeWindow) 
| where ProviderName == "MDATP" 
//Parse and expand the alert JSON 
| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) 
| mvexpand alertData 
| where alertData.Type == "file" 
//This can be expanded to include more file types 
| where alertData.Name has_any(scriptExtensions) 
| extend FileName = tostring(alertData.Name), Directory = tostring(alertData.Directory) 
| project TimeGenerated, FileName, Directory 
| join (  
W3CIISLog  
| where TimeGenerated &gt; ago(timeWindow)  
| where csUriStem has_any(scriptExtensions)  
| extend splitUriStem = split(csUriStem, "/")  
| extend FileName = splitUriStem[-1] 
| summarize StartTime=min(TimeGenerated), EndTime=max(TimeGenerated) by AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUserAgent=csUserAgent, SiteName=sSiteName, ShellLocation=csUriStem, tostring(FileName)  
) on FileName 
| project StartTime, EndTime, AttackerIP, AttackerUserAgent, SiteName, ShellLocation </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2234968-toc-hId-182623388"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Identifying Exchange&nbsp;Servers &amp; Associated&nbsp;Security Alerts</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Exchange servers can&nbsp;be challenging to identify in&nbsp;default log data;&nbsp;however&nbsp;using data available in W3CIISLog,&nbsp;Exchange servers can be identified using predictable URI strings without relying&nbsp;on the&nbsp;hostname or site name.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The query below&nbsp;extracts&nbsp;the host name from W3CIISLog where a known&nbsp;Exchange URI path is observed, this provides a list of hostnames that are running Exchange. This list of host names can then be used to&nbsp;aggregate information from the&nbsp;alerts in the&nbsp;SecurityAlert&nbsp;table.&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-csharp"><code>W3CIISLog 
| where csUriStem has_any("/owa/auth/", "/ecp/healthcheck.htm", "/ews/exchange.asmx") 
| summarize by computer=tolower(Computer) 
| join kind=leftouter ( 
SecurityAlert 
| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) 
| mvexpand alertData 
| where alertData.Type == "host" 
| extend computer = iff(isnotempty(alertData.DnsDomain), tolower(strcat(tostring(alertData.HostName), "." , tostring(alertData.DnsDomain))),tolower(tostring(alertData.HostName))) 
| summarize Alerts=dcount(SystemAlertId), AlertTimes=make_list(TimeGenerated), AlertNames=make_list(AlertName) by computer 
) on computer 
| project ExchangeServer=computer, Alerts, AlertTimes, AlertNames </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="Capture.PNG"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image Capture.PNG"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yMjM0OTY4LTI2Njk3M2k2NUI4NzlBNzBGQjc2QkI3?image-dimensions=848x162&amp;revision=6" width="848" height="162" alt="Capture.PNG" /></button></span></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The results of the query provide insights into&nbsp;whether&nbsp;additional security alerts beyond web shell alerts have been observed on the host.&nbsp;Following deployment of a web shell it’s highly likely the threat actor will begin to execute further commands on the server, triggering additional alerts.&nbsp;In the above example three Exchange servers were observed with security alerts.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">This same technique can be used to locate other web applications&nbsp;within the network that use common or predictable web paths.</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="1" id="community-2234968-toc-hId--1624831075"><SPAN data-contrast="none">W3CIISLog Analysis</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:240,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><A href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/azure-monitor/reference/tables/w3ciislog" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">W3CIISLog</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;provides detailed logging on actions performed on Microsoft&nbsp;Internet Information Servers (IIS).&nbsp;Even when an&nbsp;Endpoint detection&nbsp;alert is not&nbsp;available,&nbsp;it is possible to explore W3CIISLogs for indicators of compromise.&nbsp;W3CIISLog can also provide additional insights into which hosts&nbsp;in the network&nbsp;are web application servers.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><I><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Note:&nbsp;As part of the original Microsoft&nbsp;</SPAN></I><A href="https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/03/02/hafnium-targeting-exchange-servers/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><I><SPAN data-contrast="none">HAFNIUM blog post</SPAN></I></A><I><SPAN data-contrast="auto">, several hunting and detection queries were created to search for&nbsp;artefacts specific to the use of recent vulnerabilities.</SPAN></I><I></I></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H3 aria-level="2" id="community-2234968-toc-hId--934269601"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Identifying&nbsp;generic exploitation activity</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">If the URI associated with the vulnerable file on the server is known,&nbsp;a query can be constructed to&nbsp;identify log entries that match the URI pattern.&nbsp;W3CIIS&nbsp;logging&nbsp;stores the URI in the column&nbsp;named&nbsp;“csUriStem”, the below query can be used to search for a specific URI&nbsp;in&nbsp;logs and provide information on which clients have accessed them.&nbsp;Local IP addresses have been removed.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-csharp"><code>W3CIISLog 
| where TimeGenerated &gt; ago(3d) 
| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) 
//Insert potentially exploited URI here 
| where csUriStem =~ "/owa/auth/x.js" 
| project TimeGenerated, sSiteName, csMethod, csUriStem, sPort, cIP, csUserAgent </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="Capture2.PNG"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image Capture2.PNG"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yMjM0OTY4LTI2Njk4NGlGNTRDQjAxMjI2ODkyN0U1?image-dimensions=983x107&amp;revision=6" width="983" height="107" alt="Capture2.PNG" /></button></span></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">For HAFNIUM attacks observed by MSTIC an indicator feed has been<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW114351314 BCX8" href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/tree/master/Sample%20Data/Feeds" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">made available</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>(</SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW114351314 BCX8" href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/master/Sample%20Data/Feeds/MSTICIoCs-ExchangeServerVulnerabilitiesDisclosedMarch2021.csv" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">CSV</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">,<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW114351314 BCX8" href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/master/Sample%20Data/Feeds/MSTICIoCs-ExchangeServerVulnerabilitiesDisclosedMarch2021.json" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">JSON</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">)</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">. A</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>detection query</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>that<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">will check for the presence of indicators in multiple data sources</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">, has also been made available by the Azure Sentinel team</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">. The<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">detection</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>can be found<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW114351314 BCX8" href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/blob/6af6b23336df36e475786e2fc946cd7fd8c3de35/Detections/MultipleDataSources/ExchangeServerVulnerabilitiesMarch2021IoCs.yaml" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">here</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8">, and IOC’s</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>released as feeds by MSTIC</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>can be found in this<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW114351314 BCX8" href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/tree/master/Sample%20Data/Feeds" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">directory</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW114351314 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8">The recent<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8">E</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8">xchange vulnerabilities<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8">do not need to be targeted at a specific file</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8">.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>Analysis of automated exploitation tools online shows that many randomise the filenames used</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8">;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144220947 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>this means that no legitimate user will visit these files as they do not exist on the server. As these filenames are randomly generated, static string matching cannot be used.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW144220947 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW144220947 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8">T</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8">he Kusto “matches_regex” function can be used to perform regular expression matching on URI’s. The below example extracts events</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>where the URI matches<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8">files associated with the exploitation of<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8">CVE-2021-27065</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144657508 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>from W3CIISLog.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW144657508 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-csharp"><code>W3CIISLog 
| where TimeGenerated &gt; ago(3d) 
| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) 
| where (csUriStem matches regex @"\/owa\/auth\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\.js") or (csUriStem matches regex @"\/ecp\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\.(js|flt|css)") 
| project TimeGenerated, sSiteName, csMethod, csUriStem, sPort, cIP, csUserAgent</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="Capture2.PNG"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image Capture2.PNG"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yMjM0OTY4LTI2Njk4NWkzRDlCMTk0MDA0RjFEMjIz?image-dimensions=983x107&amp;revision=6" width="983" height="107" alt="Capture2.PNG" /></button></span></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW237299863 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW237299863 BCX8">The previous queries can be limited when the files being exploited a</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW237299863 BCX8">re</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW237299863 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>commonly accessed. They would produce many candidate attacker IP addresses, making analysis</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW237299863 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>challenging.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW237299863 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun CommentStart SCXW15033289 BCX8">Using the recent Exchange vulnerabilities as an example,<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">Microsoft has<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">seen</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>malicious<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">a</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">utomated</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>tools</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">released publicly that are being<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">used&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">to</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>exploit<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">the Exchange</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">vulnerabilities</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">. Thes</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">e tools are designed to<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">only visit</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">specific</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">URIs on the server that are required to perform the exploit. This activity differs from<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">normal and<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">legitimate Administrator or User<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">application<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">browsing<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">activity</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">and if observed should be investigated</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW15033289 BCX8">.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW15033289 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW15033289 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">It is possible to craft a query that uses basic statistical analysis to identify instances where a client has visited a disproportionately high number of exploit-related URI’s when compared to other URIs on the site.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">,<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">The query below calculates the</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>total number of suspicious URIs<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">that<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">have been visited by each user, it then calculates the total number of URIs visited by the user. Where the number of exploit<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">related<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">URIs is<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">a significant proportion of URIs visited, a result is returned.<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun CommentStart SCXW187221405 BCX8">By<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8">default,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187221405 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>the query requires over 90% of the URIs visited by the user to be suspicious.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW187221405 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-csharp"><code>let timeRange = 7d;
//Calculate number of suspicious URI stems visited by user 
W3CIISLog
| where TimeGenerated &gt; ago(timeRange)
| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) 
| where (csUriStem matches regex @"\/owa\/auth\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\.js") or (csUriStem matches regex @"\/ecp\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\.(js|flt|css)") or (csUriStem =~ "/ews/exchange.asmx") 
| extend userHash = hash_md5(strcat(cIP, csUserAgent)) 
| summarize susCount=dcount(csUriStem), make_list(csUriStem), min(TimeGenerated), max(TimeGenerated) by userHash, cIP, csUserAgent 
| join kind=leftouter  ( 
//Calculate unique URI stems visited by each user 
W3CIISLog 
| where TimeGenerated &gt; ago(timeRange) 
| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP))
| extend userHash = hash_md5(strcat(cIP, csUserAgent)) 
| summarize allCount=dcount(csUriStem) by userHash 
) on userHash 
//Find instances where only a common endpoint was seen 
| extend containsDefault = iff(list_csUriStem contains "/ews/exchange.asmx", 1, 0) 
//If we only see the common endpoint and nothing else dump it 
| extend result = iff(containsDefault == 1, containsDefault+susCount, 0) 
| where result != 2 
| extend susPercentage = susCount / allCount * 100 
| where susPercentage &gt; 90 
| project StartTime=min_TimeGenerated, EndTime=max_TimeGenerated, AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUA=csUserAgent, URIsVisited=list_csUriStem, suspiciousPercentage=susPercentage, allUriCount=allCount, suspiciousUriCount=susCount</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW203166830 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW203166830 BCX8">While this query is designed to detect recent Exchange exploit activity, it can be easily adapted to<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW203166830 BCX8">other exploit chains if the pages or URIs used are known.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW203166830 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H3 id="community-2234968-toc-hId-1553243232"><SPAN class="EOP SCXW203166830 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap" data-ccp-charstyle-defn="{&quot;ObjectId&quot;:&quot;755fac67-903c-4f98-b8cb-b311087515c8|114&quot;,&quot;ClassId&quot;:1073872969,&quot;Properties&quot;:[134233614,&quot;true&quot;,201340122,&quot;1&quot;,469775450,&quot;inner-wrap&quot;,469778129,&quot;inner-wrap&quot;,469778324,&quot;Default Paragraph Font&quot;]}">Rare Client File Access</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="LineBreakBlob BlobObject DragDrop SCXW232778808 BCX8"><SPAN class="SCXW232778808 BCX8">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW203166830 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">A previously published&nbsp;<SPAN><A href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/blob/master/Hunting%20Queries/W3CIISLog/RareClientFileAccess.yaml" target="_self" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">hunti</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">n</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">g query</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW99569963" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">can be used to detect instances where resources on a server are requested by a single client</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>– a<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">behaviour</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>that should be investigated in the context of web shell</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">exploits</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">After<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">t</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">he actor<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun ContextualSpellingAndGrammarErrorV2 SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">creates<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun ContextualSpellingAndGrammarErrorV2 SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">web</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>shell<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">o</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">n</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">the</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>server</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">, it’s likely that they will be the only user to access the file</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>to complete their intended objective</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="inner-wrap">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW232778808 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="1" id="community-2234968-toc-hId-1542740128"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Investigating the Attacker</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:240,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">In the&nbsp;previous&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/azure-sentinel/web-shell-threat-hunting-with-azure-sentinel-and-microsoft/ba-p/1448065#Building%20out%20the%20investigation%20using%20Jupyter%20Notebooks" target="_blank"><SPAN data-contrast="none">blog post</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;covering SharePoint&nbsp;exploitation,&nbsp;a Jupyter&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;Guided Investigation is provided. This notebook can also be used to investigate&nbsp;on-prem&nbsp;Exchange compromises&nbsp;within your environment.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The notebook extracts&nbsp;alerts from Microsoft 365 Defender related to web shell activity,&nbsp;these can then be enriched with information from W3CIIS to identify the attacker IP and User Agent.&nbsp;The attackers IP and User Agent can be used to hunt through multiple log sources for potential post-compromise activity.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">After the attacker details have been identified,&nbsp;the notebook can be used to&nbsp;locate&nbsp;files that were accessed by the attacker prior to the web shell being installed. The notebook will also&nbsp;locate the first instance that the attacker visited the server.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><A href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel-Notebooks/blob/master/Guided%20Investigation%20-%20MDE%20Webshell%20Alerts.ipynb" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Azure-Sentinel-Notebooks/Guided Investigation - MDE Webshell Alerts.ipynb at master · Azure/Azure-Sentinel-Notebooks (github.com)</SPAN></A><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Instructions for getting the notebook up and&nbsp;running can be&nbsp;found in the&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/azure-sentinel/web-shell-threat-hunting-with-azure-sentinel-and-microsoft/ba-p/1448065#Building%20out%20the%20investigation%20using%20Jupyter%20Notebooks" target="_blank"><SPAN data-contrast="none">original blog post</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">, under the title “Building out the Investigation using Jupyter Notebooks”.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>

In the below example,\u0026nbsp;alerts containing\u0026nbsp;ASP,\u0026nbsp;ASPX, ASMX and ASAX files will be extracted;\u0026nbsp;these are web script files\u0026nbsp;commonly used\u0026nbsp;by\u0026nbsp;Exchange servers.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eAfter extracting relevant web shell alerts the query will join the alert information with the W3CIIS log, this allows the query to identify any clients that have accessed the potential shell file, allowing\u0026nbsp;the potential\u0026nbsp;attacker to be identified.\u0026nbsp;A version of the query below is already available as an Azure Sentinel detection and can be\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/blob/master/Detections/W3CIISLog/MaliciousAlertLinkedWebRequests.yaml\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"none\"\u003efound here\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003e.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"lia-code-sample language-csharp\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003elet timeWindow = 3d; \n//Script file extensions to match on, can be expanded for your environment \nlet scriptExtensions = dynamic([\".asp\", \".aspx\", \".asmx\", \".asax\"]); \nSecurityAlert \n| where TimeGenerated \u0026gt; ago(timeWindow) \n| where ProviderName == \"MDATP\" \n//Parse and expand the alert JSON \n| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) \n| mvexpand alertData \n| where alertData.Type == \"file\" \n//This can be expanded to include more file types \n| where alertData.Name has_any(scriptExtensions) \n| extend FileName = tostring(alertData.Name), Directory = tostring(alertData.Directory) \n| project TimeGenerated, FileName, Directory \n| join (  \nW3CIISLog  \n| where TimeGenerated \u0026gt; ago(timeWindow)  \n| where csUriStem has_any(scriptExtensions)  \n| extend splitUriStem = split(csUriStem, \"/\")  \n| extend FileName = splitUriStem[-1] \n| summarize StartTime=min(TimeGenerated), EndTime=max(TimeGenerated) by AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUserAgent=csUserAgent, SiteName=sSiteName, ShellLocation=csUriStem, tostring(FileName)  \n) on FileName \n| project StartTime, EndTime, AttackerIP, AttackerUserAgent, SiteName, ShellLocation \u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cH2 aria-level=\"2\" id=\"community-2234968-toc-hId-182623388\"\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"none\"\u003eIdentifying Exchange\u0026nbsp;Servers \u0026amp; Associated\u0026nbsp;Security Alerts\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559738\u0026quot;:40,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eExchange servers can\u0026nbsp;be challenging to identify in\u0026nbsp;default log data;\u0026nbsp;however\u0026nbsp;using data available in W3CIISLog,\u0026nbsp;Exchange servers can be identified using predictable URI strings without relying\u0026nbsp;on the\u0026nbsp;hostname or site name.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eThe query below\u0026nbsp;extracts\u0026nbsp;the host name from W3CIISLog where a known\u0026nbsp;Exchange URI path is observed, this provides a list of hostnames that are running Exchange. This list of host names can then be used to\u0026nbsp;aggregate information from the\u0026nbsp;alerts in the\u0026nbsp;SecurityAlert\u0026nbsp;table.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"lia-code-sample language-csharp\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eW3CIISLog \n| where csUriStem has_any(\"/owa/auth/\", \"/ecp/healthcheck.htm\", \"/ews/exchange.asmx\") \n| summarize by computer=tolower(Computer) \n| join kind=leftouter ( \nSecurityAlert \n| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) \n| mvexpand alertData \n| where alertData.Type == \"host\" \n| extend computer = iff(isnotempty(alertData.DnsDomain), tolower(strcat(tostring(alertData.HostName), \".\" , tostring(alertData.DnsDomain))),tolower(tostring(alertData.HostName))) \n| summarize Alerts=dcount(SystemAlertId), AlertTimes=make_list(TimeGenerated), AlertNames=make_list(AlertName) by computer \n) on computer \n| project ExchangeServer=computer, Alerts, AlertTimes, AlertNames class=\"lia-code-sample language-csharp\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003elet timeRange = 7d;\n//Calculate number of suspicious URI stems visited by user \nW3CIISLog\n| where TimeGenerated \u0026gt; ago(timeRange)\n| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP)) \n| where (csUriStem matches regex @\"\\/owa\\/auth\\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\\.js\") or (csUriStem matches regex @\"\\/ecp\\/[A-Za-z0-9]{1,30}\\.(js|flt|css)\") or (csUriStem =~ \"/ews/exchange.asmx\") \n| extend userHash = hash_md5(strcat(cIP, csUserAgent)) \n| summarize susCount=dcount(csUriStem), make_list(csUriStem), min(TimeGenerated), max(TimeGenerated) by userHash, cIP, csUserAgent \n| join kind=leftouter  ( \n//Calculate unique URI stems visited by each user \nW3CIISLog \n| where TimeGenerated \u0026gt; ago(timeRange) \n| where not(ipv4_is_private(cIP))\n| extend userHash = hash_md5(strcat(cIP, csUserAgent)) \n| summarize allCount=dcount(csUriStem) by userHash \n) on userHash \n//Find instances where only a common endpoint was seen \n| extend containsDefault = iff(list_csUriStem contains \"/ews/exchange.asmx\", 1, 0) \n//If we only see the common endpoint and nothing else dump it \n| extend result = iff(containsDefault == 1, containsDefault+susCount, 0) \n| where result != 2 \n| extend susPercentage = susCount / allCount * 100 \n| where susPercentage \u0026gt; 90 \n| project StartTime=min_TimeGenerated, EndTime=max_TimeGenerated, AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUA=csUserAgent, URIsVisited=list_csUriStem, suspiciousPercentage=susPercentage, allUriCount=allCount, In the below example,\u0026nbsp;alerts containing\u0026nbsp;ASP,\u0026nbsp;ASPX, ASMX and ASAX files will be extracted;\u0026nbsp;these are web script files\u0026nbsp;commonly used\u0026nbsp;by\u0026nbsp;Exchange servers.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eAfter extracting relevant web shell alerts the query will join the alert information with the W3CIIS log, this allows the query to identify any clients that have accessed the potential shell file, allowing\u0026nbsp;the potential\u0026nbsp;attacker to be identified.\u0026nbsp;A version of the query below is already available as an Azure Sentinel detection and can be\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel/blob/master/Detections/W3CIISLog/MaliciousAlertLinkedWebRequests.yaml\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"none\"\u003efound here\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003e.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cLI-CODE lang=\"csharp\"\u003elet timeWindow = 3d; \n//Script file extensions to match on, can be expanded for your environment \nlet scriptExtensions = dynamic([\".asp\", \".aspx\", \".asmx\", \".asax\"]); \nSecurityAlert \n| where TimeGenerated \u0026gt; ago(timeWindow) \n| where ProviderName == \"MDATP\" \n//Parse and expand the alert JSON \n| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) \n| mvexpand alertData \n| where alertData.Type == \"file\" \n//This can be expanded to include more file types \n| where alertData.Name has_any(scriptExtensions) \n| extend FileName = tostring(alertData.Name), Directory = tostring(alertData.Directory) \n| project TimeGenerated, FileName, Directory \n| join (  \nW3CIISLog  \n| where TimeGenerated \u0026gt; ago(timeWindow)  \n| where csUriStem has_any(scriptExtensions)  \n| extend splitUriStem = split(csUriStem, \"/\")  \n| extend FileName = splitUriStem[-1] \n| summarize StartTime=min(TimeGenerated), EndTime=max(TimeGenerated) by AttackerIP=cIP, AttackerUserAgent=csUserAgent, SiteName=sSiteName, ShellLocation=csUriStem, tostring(FileName)  \n) on FileName \n| project StartTime, EndTime, AttackerIP, AttackerUserAgent, SiteName, ShellLocation \u003c/LI-CODE\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cH2 aria-level=\"2\"\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"none\"\u003eIdentifying Exchange\u0026nbsp;Servers \u0026amp; Associated\u0026nbsp;Security Alerts\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559738\u0026quot;:40,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eExchange servers can\u0026nbsp;be challenging to identify in\u0026nbsp;default log data;\u0026nbsp;however\u0026nbsp;using data available in W3CIISLog,\u0026nbsp;Exchange servers can be identified using predictable URI strings without relying\u0026nbsp;on the\u0026nbsp;hostname or site name.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eThe query below\u0026nbsp;extracts\u0026nbsp;the host name from W3CIISLog where a known\u0026nbsp;Exchange URI path is observed, this provides a list of hostnames that are running Exchange. This list of host names can then be used to\u0026nbsp;aggregate information from the\u0026nbsp;alerts in the\u0026nbsp;SecurityAlert\u0026nbsp;table.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cLI-CODE lang=\"csharp\"\u003eW3CIISLog \n| where csUriStem has_any(\"/owa/auth/\", \"/ecp/healthcheck.htm\", \"/ews/exchange.asmx\") \n| summarize by computer=tolower(Computer) \n| join kind=leftouter ( \nSecurityAlert \n| extend alertData = parse_json(Entities) \n| mvexpand alertData \n| where alertData.Type == \"host\" \n| extend computer = iff(isnotempty(alertData.DnsDomain), tolower(strcat(tostring(alertData.HostName), \".\" , tostring(alertData.DnsDomain))),tolower(tostring(alertData.HostName))) \n| summarize Alerts=dcount(SystemAlertId), AlertTimes=make_list(TimeGenerated), AlertNames=make_list(AlertName) by computer \n) on computer \n| project ExchangeServer=computer, Alerts, AlertTimes, AlertNames \u003c/LI-CODE\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u003cLI-IMAGE width=\"848\" height=\"162\" alt=\"Capture.PNG\" data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eIf the URI associated with the vulnerable file on the server is known,\u0026nbsp;a query can be constructed to\u0026nbsp;identify log entries that match the URI pattern.\u0026nbsp;W3CIIS\u0026nbsp;logging\u0026nbsp;stores the URI in the column\u0026nbsp;named\u0026nbsp;“csUriStem”, the below query can be used to search for a specific data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cLI-CODE project TimeGenerated, sSiteName, csMethod, csUriStem, sPort, cIP, csUserAgent
